class="firstHeading" lang="en">Great Famine (Ireland)</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Famine in Ireland between 1845 and 1852</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Irish famine" redirects here. For other famines in Ireland, see <a href="/wiki/Irish_famine_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Irish famine (disambiguation)">Irish famine (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n\n</p>\n<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold"><span class="fn org">Great Famine</span><br /><i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">an Gorta M\xc3\xb3r/Drochshaol</i></i></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a href="/wiki/File:Skibbereen_by_James_Mahony,_1847.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Skibbereen by James Mahony, 1847.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Skibbereen_by_James_Mahony%2C_1847.JPG/360px-Skibbereen_by_James_Mahony%2C_1847.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/97/Skibbereen_by_James_Mahony%2C_1847.JPG 2x" data-file-width="405" data-file-height="560" /></a><div>Scene at <a href="/wiki/Skibbereen" title="Skibbereen">Skibbereen</a> during the Great Famine, by <a href="/wiki/County_Cork" title="County Cork">Cork</a> artist James Mahony (1810\xe2\x80\x931879), commissioned by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Illustrated_London_News" title="The Illustrated London News">The Illustrated London News</a></i>, 1847.</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Country</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland</a></td></tr><tr><th deaths</th><td>\n1 million</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Observations</th><td>\nPolicy failure, <a href="/wiki/Phytophthora_infestans" title="Phytophthora infestans">potato blight</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corn_Laws" title="Corn Laws">Corn Laws</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Relief</th><td>\n<a href="#Charity">see below</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Impact on demographics</th><td>\nPopulation fell by 20\xe2\x80\x9325% due to mortality and emigration</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Consequences</th><td>\nPermanent change in the country\'s demographic, memorials to the Great Famine</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Preceded by</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Irish_Famine_(1740%E2%80%9341)" title="Irish Famine (1740\xe2\x80\x9341)">Irish Famine (1740\xe2\x80\x9341)</a> (<i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">Bliain an \xc3\x81ir</i></i>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Succeeded by</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Irish_Famine_(1879)" title="Irish Famine (1879)">Irish Famine, 1879</a> (<i><i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">An Gorta Beag</i></i>)</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Great Famine</b> (<a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga">an Gorta M\xc3\xb3r</i>, <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Irish" title="Help:IPA/Irish">[an\xcb\xa0 \xcb\x88g\xc9\x94\xc9\xbe\xcb\xa0t\xcc\xaa\xcb\xa0a m\xcb\xa0o\xcb\x90\xc9\xbe\xcb\xa0]</a></span>) or the <b>Great Hunger</b> was a period of mass starvation, disease, and emigration in Ireland between 1845 and 1849.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinealy1994xv_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinealy1994xv-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> With the greatest impacted areas to the west and south of Ireland, where the  <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Irish_language#Nineteenth_and_twentieth_centuries" title="History of the Irish language">Irish language was primarily spoken</a>, the period was contemporaneously known as in <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga">An Drochshaol</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> loosely translated as the hard-times (or literally, "The Bad Life"). The worst year of the period, that of "Black 47", is known as <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga">Bliain an Drochshaoil</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>  During the famine, about one million people died and a million more <a href="/wiki/Emigration" title="Emigration">emigrated</a> from Ireland,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoss2002226_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoss2002226-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> causing the island\'s population to fall by between 20% and 25%.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinealy1994357_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinealy1994357-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sharing much in common with the similar <a href="/wiki/Famine_in_India#British_rule" title="Famine in India">famines in India under British rule</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Proximate_and_ultimate_causation" title="Proximate and ultimate causation">proximate cause</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a> was a natural event, a <a href="/wiki/Phytophthora_infestans" title="Phytophthora infestans">potato blight</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE\xc3\x93_Gr\xc3\xa1da20067_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE\xc3\x93_Gr\xc3\xa1da20067-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> which infected potato crops <a href="/wiki/European_Potato_Failure" title="European Potato Failure">throughout Europe</a> during the 1840s, precipitating some 100,000 deaths in total in the worst affected and similar tenant farmers of Europe, the food crisis was to influence much of the unrest in the more widespead European <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">Revolutions of 1848</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The event is sometimes referred to as the <b>Irish Potato Famine</b>, mostly outside Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinealy19945_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinealy19945-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEO&#39;Neill20091_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO&#39;Neill20091-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The famine was a watershed in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ireland" title="History of Ireland">history of Ireland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinealy1994xv_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinealy1994xv-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> which was then part of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland</a>. The Great Famine in Ireland was together with the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, to produce the greatest loss of life in 19th-century Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-maps_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maps-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The famine and its effects permanently changed the island\'s demographic, political, and cultural landscape, producing an estimated two million refugees and spurring <a href="/wiki/Irish_population_analysis" title="Irish population analysis">a century-long population decline</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-maps_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maps-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> For both the <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">native Irish</a> and those in the resulting <a href="/wiki/Irish_diaspora" title="Irish diaspora">diaspora</a>, the famine entered <a href="/wiki/Folk_memory" title="Folk memory">folk memory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinealy1994342_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinealy1994342-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The already strained <a href="/wiki/Ireland%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="Ireland\xe2\x80\x93United Kingdom relations">relations</a> between many Irish and the <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">British Crown</a> soured further both during and after the famine, heightening ethnic and sectarian tensions, and boosting <a href="/wiki/Irish_nationalism" title="Irish nationalism">Irish nationalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Irish_republicanism" title="Irish republicanism">republicanism</a> in Ireland and among Irish emigrants in the United States and elsewhere. \n</p><p>The potato blight would return to Europe in 1879 though by then the labourers of Ireland had in the <a href="/wiki/Legacy_of_the_Great_Irish_Famine" title="Legacy of the Great Irish Famine">Legacy of the Great Irish Famine</a>, begun the "<a href="/wiki/Land_War" title="Land War">Land War</a>", described as one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Agrarianism" title="Agrarianism">agrarian</a> movements to take place in 19th-century Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> the movement organized by the <a href="/wiki/Land_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Land League">Land League</a>, continued the political campaign for the <a href="/wiki/Tenant_Right_League" title="Tenant Right League">Tenant Right League</a>\'s 1850 issued <a href="/wiki/Three_Fs" title="Three Fs">Three Fs</a>, initially penned during the Great Famine. The League once the potato blight returned in 1879 <a href="/wiki/Boycott#Etymology" title="Boycott">boycotted</a> "notorious landlords" and members physically blocked evictions of farmers, with this reduction in homelessness and <a href="/wiki/House_demolition#Counter-insurgency_and_collective_punishment" title="House demolition">house demolition</a>, resulting in a drastic reduction in the number of casualties caused during <a href="/wiki/Irish_Famine_(1879)" title="Irish Famine (1879)">the following famine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-historyplace_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyplace-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bitesize_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bitesize-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox"
